bnx2x_reg.h
00001 /* bnx2x_reg.h: Broadcom Everest network driver.
00002  *
00003  * Copyright (c) 2007-2009 Broadcom Corporation
00004  *
00005  * This program is free software; you can redistribute it and/or modify
00006  * it under the terms of the GNU General Public License as published by
00007  * the Free Software Foundation.
00008  *
00009  * The registers description starts with the register Access type followed
00010  * by size in bits. For example [RW 32]. The access types are:
00011  * R  - Read only
00012  * RC - Clear on read
00013  * RW - Read/Write
00014  * ST - Statistics register (clear on read)
00015  * W  - Write only
00016  * WB - Wide bus register - the size is over 32 bits and it should be
00017  *      read/write in consecutive 32 bits accesses
00018  * WR - Write Clear (write 1 to clear the bit)
00019  *
00020  */
00021 
00022 
00023 /* [R 19] Interrupt register #0 read */
00024 #define BRB1_REG_BRB1_INT_STS                    0x6011c
00025 /* [RW 4] Parity mask register #0 read/write */
00026 #define BRB1_REG_BRB1_PRTY_MASK                  0x60138
00027 /* [R 4] Parity register #0 read */
00028 #define BRB1_REG_BRB1_PRTY_STS                   0x6012c
00029 /* [RW 10] At address BRB1_IND_FREE_LIST_PRS_CRDT initialize free head. At
00030    address BRB1_IND_FREE_LIST_PRS_CRDT+1 initialize free tail. At address
00031    BRB1_IND_FREE_LIST_PRS_CRDT+2 initialize parser initial credit. */
00032 #define BRB1_REG_FREE_LIST_PRS_CRDT              0x60200
00033 /* [RW 10] The number of free blocks above which the High_llfc signal to
00034    interface #n is de-asserted. */
00035 #define BRB1_REG_HIGH_LLFC_HIGH_THRESHOLD_0          0x6014c
00036 /* [RW 10] The number of free blocks below which the High_llfc signal to
00037    interface #n is asserted. */
00038 #define BRB1_REG_HIGH_LLFC_LOW_THRESHOLD_0           0x6013c
00039 /* [RW 23] LL RAM data. */
00040 #define BRB1_REG_LL_RAM                      0x61000
00041 /* [RW 10] The number of free blocks above which the Low_llfc signal to
00042    interface #n is de-asserted. */
00043 #define BRB1_REG_LOW_LLFC_HIGH_THRESHOLD_0           0x6016c
00044 /* [RW 10] The number of free blocks below which the Low_llfc signal to
00045    interface #n is asserted. */
00046 #define BRB1_REG_LOW_LLFC_LOW_THRESHOLD_0            0x6015c
00047 /* [R 24] The number of full blocks. */
00048 #define BRB1_REG_NUM_OF_FULL_BLOCKS              0x60090

00059 #define BRB1_REG_PAUSE_HIGH_THRESHOLD_0              0x60078
00060 #define BRB1_REG_PAUSE_HIGH_THRESHOLD_1              0x6007c

00069 #define CCM_REG_CAM_OCCUP                    0xd0188
00070 /* [RW 1] CM - CFC Interface enable. If 0 - the valid input is disregarded;
00071    acknowledge output is deasserted; all other signals are treated as usual;
00072    if 1 - normal activity. */
00073 #define CCM_REG_CCM_CFC_IFEN                     0xd003c
00074 /* [RW 1] CM - QM Interface enable. If 0 - the acknowledge input is

00076    if 1 - normal activity. */

00080 #define CCM_REG_CCM_CQM_USE_Q                    0xd00c0

00135 #define CCM_REG_CQM_INIT_CRD                     0xd020c

00139 #define CCM_REG_CQM_P_WEIGHT                     0xd00b8

00150 #define CCM_REG_CSDM_LENGTH_MIS                  0xd0170

00162    credit counter. Must be initialized to 64 at start-up. */
00163 #define CCM_REG_FIC0_INIT_CRD                    0xd0210

00168 /* [RW 1] Arbitration between Input Arbiter groups: 0 - fair Round-Robin; 1
00169    - strict priority defined by ~ccm_registers_gr_ag_pr.gr_ag_pr;
00170    ~ccm_registers_gr_ld0_pr.gr_ld0_pr and
00171    ~ccm_registers_gr_ld1_pr.gr_ld1_pr. Groups are according to channels and
00172    outputs to STORM: aggregation; load FIC0; load FIC1 and store. */
00173 #define CCM_REG_GR_ARB_TYPE                  0xd015c
00174 /* [RW 2] Load (FIC0) channel group priority. The lowest priority is 0; the
00175    highest priority is 3. It is supposed; that the Store channel priority is
00176    the compliment to 4 of the rest priorities - Aggregation channel; Load
00177    (FIC0) channel and Load (FIC1). */
00178 #define CCM_REG_GR_LD0_PR                    0xd0164
00179 /* [RW 2] Load (FIC1) channel group priority. The lowest priority is 0; the
00180    highest priority is 3. It is supposed; that the Store channel priority is
00181    the compliment to 4 of the rest priorities - Aggregation channel; Load
00182    (FIC0) channel and Load (FIC1). */
00183 #define CCM_REG_GR_LD1_PR                    0xd0168
00184 /* [RW 2] General flags index. */
00185 #define CCM_REG_INV_DONE_Q                   0xd0108
00186 /* [RW 4] The number of double REG-pairs(128 bits); loaded from the STORM
00187    context and sent to STORM; for a specific connection type. The double
00188    REG-pairs are used in order to align to STORM context row size of 128
00189    bits. The offset of these data in the STORM context is always 0. Index
00190    _(0..15) stands for the connection type (one of 16). */
00191 #define CCM_REG_N_SM_CTX_LD_0                    0xd004c

01229 /* [RW 32] The following driver registers(1...16) represent 16 drivers and
01230    32 clients. Each client can be controlled by one driver only. One in each
01231    bit represent that this driver control the appropriate client (Ex: bit 5
01232    is set means this driver control client number 5). addr1 = set; addr0 =
01233    clear; read from both addresses will give the same result = status. write
01234    to address 1 will set a request to control all the clients that their
01235    appropriate bit (in the write command) is set. if the client is free (the
01236    appropriate bit in all the other drivers is clear) one will be written to
01237    that driver register; if the client isn't free the bit will remain zero.
01238    if the appropriate bit is set (the driver request to gain control on a
01239    client it already controls the ~MISC_REGISTERS_INT_STS.GENERIC_SW
01240    interrupt will be asserted). write to address 0 will set a request to
01241    free all the clients that their appropriate bit (in the write command) is
01242    set. if the appropriate bit is clear (the driver request to free a client
01243    it doesn't controls the ~MISC_REGISTERS_INT_STS.GENERIC_SW interrupt will
01244    be asserted). */
01245 #define MISC_REG_DRIVER_CONTROL_1                0xa510
01246 #define MISC_REG_DRIVER_CONTROL_7                0xa3c8
01247 /* [RW 1] e1hmf for WOL. If clr WOL signal o the PXP will be send on bit 0
01248    only. */
01249 #define MISC_REG_E1HMF_MODE                  0xa5f8
01250 /* [RW 32] Debug only: spare RW register reset by core reset */
01251 #define MISC_REG_GENERIC_CR_0                    0xa460
01252 /* [RW 32] GPIO. [31-28] FLOAT port 0; [27-24] FLOAT port 0; When any of
01253    these bits is written as a '1'; the corresponding SPIO bit will turn off
01254    it's drivers and become an input. This is the reset state of all GPIO
01255    pins. The read value of these bits will be a '1' if that last command
01256    (#SET; #CLR; or #FLOAT) for this bit was a #FLOAT. (reset value 0xff).
01257    [23-20] CLR port 1; 19-16] CLR port 0; When any of these bits is written
01258    as a '1'; the corresponding GPIO bit will drive low. The read value of
01259    these bits will be a '1' if that last command (#SET; #CLR; or #FLOAT) for
01260    this bit was a #CLR. (reset value 0). [15-12] SET port 1; 11-8] port 0;
01261    SET When any of these bits is written as a '1'; the corresponding GPIO
01262    bit will drive high (if it has that capability). The read value of these
01263    bits will be a '1' if that last command (#SET; #CLR; or #FLOAT) for this
01264    bit was a #SET. (reset value 0). [7-4] VALUE port 1; [3-0] VALUE port 0;
01265    RO; These bits indicate the read value of each of the eight GPIO pins.
01266    This is the result value of the pin; not the drive value. Writing these
01267    bits will have not effect. */
01268 #define MISC_REG_GPIO                        0xa490
01269 /* [RW 8] These bits enable the GPIO_INTs to signals event to the
01270    IGU/MCP.according to the following map: [0] p0_gpio_0; [1] p0_gpio_1; [2]
01271    p0_gpio_2; [3] p0_gpio_3; [4] p1_gpio_0; [5] p1_gpio_1; [6] p1_gpio_2;
01272    [7] p1_gpio_3; */
01273 #define MISC_REG_GPIO_EVENT_EN                   0xa2bc
01274 /* [RW 32] GPIO INT. [31-28] OLD_CLR port1; [27-24] OLD_CLR port0; Writing a
01275    '1' to these bit clears the corresponding bit in the #OLD_VALUE register.
01276    This will acknowledge an interrupt on the falling edge of corresponding
01277    GPIO input (reset value 0). [23-16] OLD_SET [23-16] port1; OLD_SET port0;
01278    Writing a '1' to these bit sets the corresponding bit in the #OLD_VALUE
01279    register. This will acknowledge an interrupt on the rising edge of
01280    corresponding SPIO input (reset value 0). [15-12] OLD_VALUE [11-8] port1;
01281    OLD_VALUE port0; RO; These bits indicate the old value of the GPIO input
01282    value. When the ~INT_STATE bit is set; this bit indicates the OLD value
01283    of the pin such that if ~INT_STATE is set and this bit is '0'; then the
01284    interrupt is due to a low to high edge. If ~INT_STATE is set and this bit
01285    is '1'; then the interrupt is due to a high to low edge (reset value 0).
01286    [7-4] INT_STATE port1; [3-0] INT_STATE RO port0; These bits indicate the
01287    current GPIO interrupt state for each GPIO pin. This bit is cleared when
01288    the appropriate #OLD_SET or #OLD_CLR command bit is written. This bit is
01289    set when the GPIO input does not match the current value in #OLD_VALUE
01290    (reset value 0). */
01291 #define MISC_REG_GPIO_INT                    0xa494
01292 /* [R 28] this field hold the last information that caused reserved
01293    attention. bits [19:0] - address; [22:20] function; [23] reserved;
01294    [27:24] the master that caused the attention - according to the following
01295    encodeing:1 = pxp; 2 = mcp; 3 = usdm; 4 = tsdm; 5 = xsdm; 6 = csdm; 7 =
01296    dbu; 8 = dmae */
01297 #define MISC_REG_GRC_RSV_ATTN                    0xa3c0
01298 /* [R 28] this field hold the last information that caused timeout
01299    attention. bits [19:0] - address; [22:20] function; [23] reserved;
01300    [27:24] the master that caused the attention - according to the following
01301    encodeing:1 = pxp; 2 = mcp; 3 = usdm; 4 = tsdm; 5 = xsdm; 6 = csdm; 7 =
01302    dbu; 8 = dmae */
01303 #define MISC_REG_GRC_TIMEOUT_ATTN                0xa3c4
01304 /* [RW 1] Setting this bit enables a timer in the GRC block to timeout any
01305    access that does not finish within
01306    ~misc_registers_grc_timout_val.grc_timeout_val cycles. When this bit is
01307    cleared; this timeout is disabled. If this timeout occurs; the GRC shall
01308    assert it attention output. */
01309 #define MISC_REG_GRC_TIMEOUT_EN                  0xa280
01310 /* [RW 28] 28 LSB of LCPLL first register; reset val = 521. inside order of
01311    the bits is: [2:0] OAC reset value 001) CML output buffer bias control;
01312    111 for +40%; 011 for +20%; 001 for 0%; 000 for -20%. [5:3] Icp_ctrl
01313    (reset value 001) Charge pump current control; 111 for 720u; 011 for
01314    600u; 001 for 480u and 000 for 360u. [7:6] Bias_ctrl (reset value 00)
01315    Global bias control; When bit 7 is high bias current will be 10 0gh; When
01316    bit 6 is high bias will be 100w; Valid values are 00; 10; 01. [10:8]
01317    Pll_observe (reset value 010) Bits to control observability. bit 10 is
01318    for test bias; bit 9 is for test CK; bit 8 is test Vc. [12:11] Vth_ctrl
01319    (reset value 00) Comparator threshold control. 00 for 0.6V; 01 for 0.54V
01320    and 10 for 0.66V. [13] pllSeqStart (reset value 0) Enables VCO tuning
01321    sequencer: 1= sequencer disabled; 0= sequencer enabled (inverted
01322    internally). [14] reserved (reset value 0) Reset for VCO sequencer is
01323    connected to RESET input directly. [15] capRetry_en (reset value 0)
01324    enable retry on cap search failure (inverted). [16] freqMonitor_e (reset
01325    value 0) bit to continuously monitor vco freq (inverted). [17]
01326    freqDetRestart_en (reset value 0) bit to enable restart when not freq
01327    locked (inverted). [18] freqDetRetry_en (reset value 0) bit to enable
01328    retry on freq det failure(inverted). [19] pllForceFdone_en (reset value
01329    0) bit to enable pllForceFdone & pllForceFpass into pllSeq. [20]
01330    pllForceFdone (reset value 0) bit to force freqDone. [21] pllForceFpass
01331    (reset value 0) bit to force freqPass. [22] pllForceDone_en (reset value
01332    0) bit to enable pllForceCapDone. [23] pllForceCapDone (reset value 0)

01372 /* [RW 32] reset reg#2; rite/read one = the specific block is out of reset;
01373    write/read zero = the specific block is in reset; addr 0-wr- the write
01374    value will be written to the register; addr 1-set - one will be written
01375    to all the bits that have the value of one in the data written (bits that
01376    have the value of zero will not be change) ; addr 2-clear - zero will be
01377    written to all the bits that have the value of one in the data written
01378    (bits that have the value of zero will not be change); addr 3-ignore;
01379    read ignore from all addr except addr 00; inside order of the bits is:

01389 #define MISC_REG_SHARED_MEM_ADDR                 0xa2b4
01390 /* [RW 32] SPIO. [31-24] FLOAT When any of these bits is written as a '1';
01391    the corresponding SPIO bit will turn off it's drivers and become an
01392    input. This is the reset state of all SPIO pins. The read value of these
01393    bits will be a '1' if that last command (#SET; #CL; or #FLOAT) for this
01394    bit was a #FLOAT. (reset value 0xff). [23-16] CLR When any of these bits
01395    is written as a '1'; the corresponding SPIO bit will drive low. The read
01396    value of these bits will be a '1' if that last command (#SET; #CLR; or
01397 #FLOAT) for this bit was a #CLR. (reset value 0). [15-8] SET When any of
01398    these bits is written as a '1'; the corresponding SPIO bit will drive
01399    high (if it has that capability). The read value of these bits will be a
01400    '1' if that last command (#SET; #CLR; or #FLOAT) for this bit was a #SET.
01401    (reset value 0). [7-0] VALUE RO; These bits indicate the read value of
01402    each of the eight SPIO pins. This is the result value of the pin; not the
01403    drive value. Writing these bits will have not effect. Each 8 bits field
01404    is divided as follows: [0] VAUX Enable; when pulsed low; enables supply
01405    from VAUX. (This is an output pin only; the FLOAT field is not applicable
01406    for this pin); [1] VAUX Disable; when pulsed low; disables supply form
01407    VAUX. (This is an output pin only; FLOAT field is not applicable for this
01408    pin); [2] SEL_VAUX_B - Control to power switching logic. Drive low to
01409    select VAUX supply. (This is an output pin only; it is not controlled by
01410    the SET and CLR fields; it is controlled by the Main Power SM; the FLOAT
01411    field is not applicable for this pin; only the VALUE fields is relevant -
01412    it reflects the output value); [3] port swap [4] spio_4; [5] spio_5; [6]
01413    Bit 0 of UMP device ID select; read by UMP firmware; [7] Bit 1 of UMP
01414    device ID select; read by UMP firmware. */
01415 #define MISC_REG_SPIO                        0xa4fc
01416 /* [RW 8] These bits enable the SPIO_INTs to signals event to the IGU/MC.
01417    according to the following map: [3:0] reserved; [4] spio_4 [5] spio_5;
01418    [7:0] reserved */
01419 #define MISC_REG_SPIO_EVENT_EN                   0xa2b8
01420 /* [RW 32] SPIO INT. [31-24] OLD_CLR Writing a '1' to these bit clears the
01421    corresponding bit in the #OLD_VALUE register. This will acknowledge an
01422    interrupt on the falling edge of corresponding SPIO input (reset value
01423    0). [23-16] OLD_SET Writing a '1' to these bit sets the corresponding bit
01424    in the #OLD_VALUE register. This will acknowledge an interrupt on the
01425    rising edge of corresponding SPIO input (reset value 0). [15-8] OLD_VALUE
01426    RO; These bits indicate the old value of the SPIO input value. When the
01427    ~INT_STATE bit is set; this bit indicates the OLD value of the pin such
01428    that if ~INT_STATE is set and this bit is '0'; then the interrupt is due
01429    to a low to high edge. If ~INT_STATE is set and this bit is '1'; then the
01430    interrupt is due to a high to low edge (reset value 0). [7-0] INT_STATE
01431    RO; These bits indicate the current SPIO interrupt state for each SPIO
01432    pin. This bit is cleared when the appropriate #OLD_SET or #OLD_CLR
01433    command bit is written. This bit is set when the SPIO input does not
01434    match the current value in #OLD_VALUE (reset value 0). */

05322 #define CDU_VALID_DATA(_cid, _region, _type)\
05323     (((_cid) << 8) | (((_region)&0xf)<<4) | (((_type)&0xf)))
05324 #define CDU_CRC8(_cid, _region, _type)\
05325     (calc_crc8(CDU_VALID_DATA(_cid, _region, _type), 0xff))
05326 #define CDU_RSRVD_VALUE_TYPE_A(_cid, _region, _type)\
05327     (0x80 | ((CDU_CRC8(_cid, _region, _type)) & 0x7f))
05328 #define CDU_RSRVD_VALUE_TYPE_B(_crc, _type)\
05329     (0x80 | ((_type)&0xf << 3) | ((CDU_CRC8(_cid, _region, _type)) & 0x7))
05330 #define CDU_RSRVD_INVALIDATE_CONTEXT_VALUE(_val) ((_val) & ~0x80)

05332 /******************************************************************************
05333  * Description:
05334  *     Calculates crc 8 on a word value: polynomial 0-1-2-8
05335  *     Code was translated from Verilog.
05336  * Return:
05337  *****************************************************************************/
05338 static inline u8 calc_crc8(u32 data, u8 crc)
05339 {
05340     u8 D[32];
05341     u8 NewCRC[8];
05342     u8 C[8];
05343     u8 crc_res;
05344     u8 i;
05345 
05346     /* split the data into 31 bits */
05347     for (i = 0; i < 32; i++) {
05348         D[i] = (u8)(data & 1);
05349         data = data >> 1;
05350     }
05351 
05352     /* split the crc into 8 bits */
05353     for (i = 0; i < 8; i++) {
05354         C[i] = crc & 1;
05355         crc = crc >> 1;
05356     }
05357 
05358     NewCRC[0] = D[31] ^ D[30] ^ D[28] ^ D[23] ^ D[21] ^ D[19] ^ D[18] ^
05359             D[16] ^ D[14] ^ D[12] ^ D[8] ^ D[7] ^ D[6] ^ D[0] ^ C[4] ^
05360             C[6] ^ C[7];
05361     NewCRC[1] = D[30] ^ D[29] ^ D[28] ^ D[24] ^ D[23] ^ D[22] ^ D[21] ^
05362             D[20] ^ D[18] ^ D[17] ^ D[16] ^ D[15] ^ D[14] ^ D[13] ^
05363             D[12] ^ D[9] ^ D[6] ^ D[1] ^ D[0] ^ C[0] ^ C[4] ^ C[5] ^
05364             C[6];
05365     NewCRC[2] = D[29] ^ D[28] ^ D[25] ^ D[24] ^ D[22] ^ D[17] ^ D[15] ^
05366             D[13] ^ D[12] ^ D[10] ^ D[8] ^ D[6] ^ D[2] ^ D[1] ^ D[0] ^
05367             C[0] ^ C[1] ^ C[4] ^ C[5];
05368     NewCRC[3] = D[30] ^ D[29] ^ D[26] ^ D[25] ^ D[23] ^ D[18] ^ D[16] ^
05369             D[14] ^ D[13] ^ D[11] ^ D[9] ^ D[7] ^ D[3] ^ D[2] ^ D[1] ^
05370             C[1] ^ C[2] ^ C[5] ^ C[6];
05371     NewCRC[4] = D[31] ^ D[30] ^ D[27] ^ D[26] ^ D[24] ^ D[19] ^ D[17] ^
05372             D[15] ^ D[14] ^ D[12] ^ D[10] ^ D[8] ^ D[4] ^ D[3] ^ D[2] ^
05373             C[0] ^ C[2] ^ C[3] ^ C[6] ^ C[7];
05374     NewCRC[5] = D[31] ^ D[28] ^ D[27] ^ D[25] ^ D[20] ^ D[18] ^ D[16] ^
05375             D[15] ^ D[13] ^ D[11] ^ D[9] ^ D[5] ^ D[4] ^ D[3] ^ C[1] ^
05376             C[3] ^ C[4] ^ C[7];
05377     NewCRC[6] = D[29] ^ D[28] ^ D[26] ^ D[21] ^ D[19] ^ D[17] ^ D[16] ^
05378             D[14] ^ D[12] ^ D[10] ^ D[6] ^ D[5] ^ D[4] ^ C[2] ^ C[4] ^
05379             C[5];
05380     NewCRC[7] = D[30] ^ D[29] ^ D[27] ^ D[22] ^ D[20] ^ D[18] ^ D[17] ^
05381             D[15] ^ D[13] ^ D[11] ^ D[7] ^ D[6] ^ D[5] ^ C[3] ^ C[5] ^
05382             C[6];
05383 
05384     crc_res = 0;
05385     for (i = 0; i < 8; i++)
05386         crc_res |= (NewCRC[i] << i);
05387 
05388     return crc_res;
05389 }
